<br>
<ol start="2">
<li>Matt is trying to keep a freely hinged door closed while Jill and Wini are on the other side trying to push it open. The door is 60 cm wide.<br>
Matt can exert a maximum force of 225 N . Jill and Wini exert forces of 200 N and 150 N at <span class="math-inline ">
<mjx-container class="MathJax" jax="SVG"><svg style="vertical-align: -0.05ex" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="3.175ex" height="1.649ex" role="img" focusable="false" viewBox="0 -707 1403.6 729"><g stroke="currentColor" fill="currentColor" stroke-width="0" transform="matrix(1 0 0 -1 0 0)"><g data-mml-node="math"><g data-mml-node="msup"><g data-mml-node="mn"><path data-c="39" d="M352 287Q304 211 232 211Q154 211 104 270T44 396Q42 412 42 436V444Q42 537 111 606Q171 666 243 666Q245 666 249 666T257 665H261Q273 665 286 663T323 651T370 619T413 560Q456 472 456 334Q456 194 396 97Q361 41 312 10T208 -22Q147 -22 108 7T68 93T121 149Q143 149 158 135T173 96Q173 78 164 65T148 49T135 44L131 43Q131 41 138 37T164 27T206 22H212Q272 22 313 86Q352 142 352 280V287ZM244 248Q292 248 321 297T351 430Q351 508 343 542Q341 552 337 562T323 588T293 615T246 625Q208 625 181 598Q160 576 154 546T147 441Q147 358 152 329T172 282Q197 248 244 248Z"></path><path data-c="30" d="M96 585Q152 666 249 666Q297 666 345 640T423 548Q460 465 460 320Q460 165 417 83Q397 41 362 16T301 -15T250 -22Q224 -22 198 -16T137 16T82 83Q39 165 39 320Q39 494 96 585ZM321 597Q291 629 250 629Q208 629 178 597Q153 571 145 525T137 333Q137 175 145 125T181 46Q209 16 250 16Q290 16 318 46Q347 76 354 130T362 333Q362 478 354 524T321 597Z" transform="translate(500, 0)"></path></g><g data-mml-node="TeXAtom" transform="translate(1000, 393.1) scale(0.707)" data-mjx-texclass="ORD"><g data-mml-node="mo"><path data-c="2218" d="M55 251Q55 328 112 386T249 444T386 388T444 249Q444 171 388 113T250 55Q170 55 113 112T55 251ZM245 403Q188 403 142 361T96 250Q96 183 141 140T250 96Q284 96 313 109T354 135T375 160Q403 197 403 250Q403 313 360 358T245 403Z"></path></g></g></g></g></g></svg></mjx-container></span> to the door.<br>
Jill exerts her force 10 cm from the edge of the door, and Wini in the middle as shown in the diagram.<br>
<img src="https://cdn.mathpix.com/cropped/2025_10_25_9e8fbe5398c75afa7e82g-1.jpg?height=253&amp;width=775&amp;top_left_y=1501&amp;top_left_x=519" alt=""></li>
</ol>
<div>Determine whether Matt can keep the door closed.</div>
<details>
<summary><span class="details-marker">&nbsp;</span><span style="color:blue">Hint</span></summary><div style="font-size: 22px;">
<div>To maximise his moment, Matt should push at the edge of the door opposite to the hinges.<br>
Careful that the unit of length need to be consistent and better convert it to metres when calculating moments in Nm.</div>
</div>
</details>
<details>
<summary><span class="details-marker">&nbsp;</span><span style="color:green">Solutions</span></summary><div style="font-size: 22px">

Matt cannot keep the door closed as <span class="math-inline ">

</details>
<br>
<ol start="3">
<li></li>
</ol>
<div><img src="https://cdn.mathpix.com/cropped/2025_10_25_9e8fbe5398c75afa7e82g-1.jpg?height=295&amp;width=912&amp;top_left_y=1941&amp;top_left_x=516" alt=""></div>
<div>A uniform rod AB of length 8 m and weight 180 N is held in horizontal equilibrium by two vertical wires. One wire is 1 m from A and the other 2 m from B .<br>
(a) Draw a diagram showing all the forces acting on the rod.</div>
<details>
<summary><span class="details-marker">&nbsp;</span><span style="color:green">Solutions</span></summary><div style="font-size: 22px">
<div>The forces acting on the rod are:</div>
<ul>
<li>The weight of the rod (180 N) acting vertically downwards at the centre of mass, which is 4 m from A .</li>
<li>The tension in the wire 1 m from A , acting vertically upwards.</li>
<li>The tension in the wire 2 m from B , acting vertically upwards.</li>
</ul>
</div>
</details>
<br>
<div>(b) Calculate the tensions in the wires.</div>
<details>
<summary><span class="details-marker">&nbsp;</span><span style="color:blue">Hint</span></summary><div style="font-size: 22px;">
<div>Can use different points to take moments about. Use centre of the rod, or use Point A, or Point B.<br>
Remember to set up equations for vertical equilibrium as well.</div>
</div>
</details>
<details>
<summary><span class="details-marker">&nbsp;</span><span style="color:green">Solutions</span></summary><div style="font-size: 22px">
<div>Let the tension in the wire 1 m from A be <span class="math-inline ">

<div><span class="math-block ">

<div>Substituting back into (2):</div>

<div>=========<br>
If use moments about center of rod:<br>
Taking moments about the center of the rod:</div>

<div>Substituting back into (3):</div>

<br>
<ol start="4">
<li>An injured climber is tied to a stretcher AB of length 2.5 m . The total mass of the climber and the stretcher is 90 kg.<br>
In this question you should make the following modelling assumptions:</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>the centre of mass, G , of the stretcher with climber is a distance 1.875 m from the end A of the stretcher, as shown in the diagram,</li>
<li>all the forces acting on the system are in the same vertical plane.<br>
<img src="https://cdn.mathpix.com/cropped/2025_10_25_9e8fbe5398c75afa7e82g-2.jpg?height=281&amp;width=1024&amp;top_left_y=699&amp;top_left_x=513" alt=""></li>
</ul>
<div>The lifting forces are each vertically upwards at the ends A and B of the stretcher, and the stretcher is held in horizontal equilibrium, as shown in the diagram above. Calculate the values of the lifting forces.</div>
<details>

627T492 637H475V683H483Q498 680 600 680Q706 680 715 683H724V637H707Q634 633 622 598L621 302V6L614 0H600Q585 0 582 3T481 150T282 443T171 605V345L172 86Q183 50 257 46H274V0H265Q250 3 150 3Q48 3 33 0H25V46H42Z"></path></g></g></g></g></svg></mjx-container></span>, acting vertically downwards at G, which is equal to sum of lifting forces at A and B.<br>
Can use Point A or Point B to take moments about.</div>
</div>
</details>

<div>Substituting the value of <span class="math-inline ">

<ol start="5">
<li></li>
</ol>
<div><img src="https://cdn.mathpix.com/cropped/2025_10_25_9e8fbe5398c75afa7e82g-2.jpg?height=227&amp;width=867&amp;top_left_y=1353&amp;top_left_x=516" alt=""></div>
<div>A uniform, horizontal, rigid shelf CD has a weight of 40 N and length 1.6 m . It is resting on two thin brackets A and B which are 0.4 m and 0.2 m respectively from C and D , as shown in the diagram above.<br>
(a) Calculate the reaction forces of the brackets on the shelf.</div>
<details>
<summary><span class="details-marker">&nbsp;</span><span style="color:blue">Hint</span></summary><div style="font-size: 22px;">
<div>Just use the principle of moments and vertical equilibrium.<br>
Reaction forces at A and B are upwards, and is equal to the weight of the shelf downwards.</div>
</div>
</details>
<details>
<summary><span class="details-marker">&nbsp;</span><span style="color:green">Solutions</span></summary><div style="font-size: 22px">
<div>Let the reaction force at A be <span class="math-inline ">

Taking moments about C :</div>

Find a similar expression for the vertical reaction force on the shelf at B.</div>
<details>
<summary><span class="details-marker">&nbsp;</span><span style="color:blue">Hint</span></summary><div style="font-size: 22px;">
<div>Similar to part (a), but now there is an additional weight W acting downwards at a distance x from C.</div>
</div>
</details>
<details>
<summary><span class="details-marker">&nbsp;</span><span style="color:green">Solutions</span></summary><div style="font-size: 22px">

<div>From (2), we have <span class="math-inline ">
<mjx-container class="MathJax" jax="SVG"><svg style="vertical-align: -0.345ex" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="19.257ex" height="1.891ex" role="img" focusable="false" viewBox="0 -683 8511.5 80V71Q602 53 603 43T614 25T640 16Q668 16 686 38T712 85Q717 99 720 102T735 105Q755 105 755 93Q755 75 731 36Q693 -21 641 -21H632Q571 -21 531 4T487 82Q487 109 502 166T517 239Q517 290 474 313Q459 320 449 <details>
<summary><span class="details-marker">&nbsp;</span><span style="color:blue">Hint</span></summary><div style="font-size: 22px;">
<div>Now need to use Point A as the pivot point to take moments about.<br>
And remember, when the shelf is just about to tip, the reaction force at B is zero, so we just need to consider the moments from weight of shelf and the object.</div>
</div>
</details>
<details>
<summary><span class="details-marker">&nbsp;</span><span style="color:green">Solutions</span></summary><div style="font-size: 22px">
<div>Taking moments about A when the shelf is just about to tip:</div>
